  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_24aaf63c-80bb-4462-b2e6-77d5c784fc1e'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer14339714580427588251">Like a surreal and highly caffeinated version of <i>The Big Chill</i>, Jonathan Coe's new novel follows four students who knew each other in college in the eighties. Sarah is a narcoleptic who has dreams so vivid she mistakes them for real events. Robert has his life changed forever by the misunderstandings that arise from her condition. Terry spends his wakeful nights fueling hi</span>
  <span id="freeText14339714580427588251" style="display:none">Like a surreal and highly caffeinated version of <i>The Big Chill</i>, Jonathan Coe's new novel follows four students who knew each other in college in the eighties. Sarah is a narcoleptic who has dreams so vivid she mistakes them for real events. Robert has his life changed forever by the misunderstandings that arise from her condition. Terry spends his wakeful nights fueling his obsession with movies. And an increasingly unstable doctor, Gregory, sees sleep as a life-shortening disease which he must eradicate.<br /><br />But after ten years of fretful slumber and dreams gone bad, the four reunite in their college town to confront their disorders. In a Gothic cliffside manor being used as a clinic for sleep disorders, they discover that neither love, nor lunacy, nor obsession ever rests.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14339714580427588251" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/465396-so-i-just-finished-reading-house-of">So, I just finished reading House of Sleep, and I&#39;m puzzling over the opening. Just who is it who shouts &quot;Bitch&quot; on the first page? I&#39;ve gone over the book twice, remembering that it comes of/is hinted at later, but have come up empty. Would love any help answering this question.</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_465396'><a id="like_count_community_question_465396" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/465396?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">1 like</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F89055.The_House_of_Sleep">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/465396-so-i-just-finished-reading-house-of">5 years ago</a>
</li>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/29707113-wiz"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1395481229i/29707113._UY100_CR33,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/29707113-wiz">Wiz</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I believe it's a simply a random stranger, although there is also the inference (made by Gregory soon after) that it may have been one of Sarah's vivi<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I believe it's a simply a random stranger, although there is also the inference (made by Gregory soon after) that it may have been one of Sarah's vivid dreams that she mistook for reality. Personally, I go with the theory that it DID happen but that it also conveniently acts as a plot device to introduce the idea of Sarah's narcolepsy and the novel's subsequent themes of reality/interpretation/illusion. If you look at the author's note that prefaces the book, all the odd numbered chapters take place in one period of the novel's chronology and the even numbered ones at a later date. Thus, it would not have been possible for this to have been Sarah's husband who she did not meet until she left Ashdown,<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_109852151" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/109852151" />
    <a title="Boyd" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1907260-boyd"><img alt="Boyd" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1238131658p2/1907260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/109852151?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Boyd" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Boyd" href="/user/show/1907260-boyd">Boyd</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer109852151" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1946874790784763025">Jonathan Coe, as he has demonstrated many times, is an agile and humane writer, and this book is perfectly readable and fitfully affecting. However, it's not the complex masterpiece it's touted as being. What has been described as an intricate structure is, in reality, a protracted series of coincidences that carries on right to the end. The central plot twist can be seen coming a mile away, and the four or five main characters' lives intersect in so many ways that you'd think they were the only</span>
  <span id="freeText1946874790784763025" style="display:none">Jonathan Coe, as he has demonstrated many times, is an agile and humane writer, and this book is perfectly readable and fitfully affecting. However, it's not the complex masterpiece it's touted as being. What has been described as an intricate structure is, in reality, a protracted series of coincidences that carries on right to the end. The central plot twist can be seen coming a mile away, and the four or five main characters' lives intersect in so many ways that you'd think they were the only people on earth. It's like one of those nineteenth-century operas in which someone puts on a mask or switches clothing, and suddenly nobody recognizes him anymore. But at least in opera, there's the music.<br /><br />Coe handles the alternating-chapter format gracefully, and I like the conceit of the sleep clinic: it's the reason I got hold of the book to begin with. The execution doesn't live up to the idea, though, and even a mad scientist can't perk it up--rather the reverse. I had high hopes for the "missing film masterpiece" plot thread, too; but Coe, having brought it up, doesn't do much with it. <br /><br />Some missed opportunities here, I'd say. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1946874790784763025" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1467702232" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1467702232" />
    <a title="Chris_P" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44309339-chris-p"><img alt="Chris_P" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558554241p2/44309339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1467702232?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris_P" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris_P" href="/user/show/44309339-chris-p">Chris_P</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1467702232" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5789985066941666533">"The House of Sleep" provides a unique reading experience, that's for sure. Its very structure resembles sleep, as the chapters are named after the stages one goes through when sleeping. Hence, reading it, you actually feel like sinking into a restless sleep full of dreams. <br/><br/>Coe has made a hell of a job with the characters. Each has their own path to follow, their own issues, fears and complications. Yet they affect each other's lives in extraordinary manners. One thing they all have in common th</span>
  <span id="freeText5789985066941666533" style="display:none">"The House of Sleep" provides a unique reading experience, that's for sure. Its very structure resembles sleep, as the chapters are named after the stages one goes through when sleeping. Hence, reading it, you actually feel like sinking into a restless sleep full of dreams. <br /><br />Coe has made a hell of a job with the characters. Each has their own path to follow, their own issues, fears and complications. Yet they affect each other's lives in extraordinary manners. One thing they all have in common though, is that none of them is entirely happy with who they are. The narrative is a bit tricky and you have to be really thorough in order not to miss important plot points. That's something I generally like in books and films, that is when the creators treat their audience as thinking, intelligent people. However, I'd be lying if I said that it left me with no questions. I'm convinced that it was Coe's intention to leave some things up to the reader's judgement. Like how come the very building that housed the protagonists' school years was turned into the sleep disorder clinic that would bring them back together? And it's not just that. The coincidences are just too many, while some of them give the story a metaphysical feeling. Like the one with the photo and Robert's dream (those of you who've read it know what I'm talking about). Or some recurring events that shouldn't be... recurring. But wait... that reminds me of something...</span>
  <a data-text-id="5789985066941666533" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_44147167" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/44147167" />
    <a title="El" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/83144-el"><img alt="El" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479156984p2/83144.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/44147167?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="El" class="user" itemprop="url" name="El" href="/user/show/83144-el">El</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=20th-centurylit-late">20th-centurylit-late</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer44147167" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13509419663809644422">Sometimes I think there must be something broken inside my head, for often as I read books which are labeled "funny", "hilarious", "silly" I find myself rarely cracking a smile during my reading. In fact, I am often so distracted by the idea that it is labeled as such that I am downright disturbed that anyone would find humor in the work. This is one of those books.<br/><br/>Maybe to some sleep disorders are funny, maybe narcoleptics say and do funny things (losing ones job due to narcolepsy must be the "</span>
  <span id="freeText13509419663809644422" style="display:none">Sometimes I think there must be something broken inside my head, for often as I read books which are labeled "funny", "hilarious", "silly" I find myself rarely cracking a smile during my reading. In fact, I am often so distracted by the idea that it is labeled as such that I am downright disturbed that anyone would find humor in the work. This is one of those books.<br /><br />Maybe to some sleep disorders are funny, maybe narcoleptics say and do funny things (losing ones job due to narcolepsy must be the "hilarious" bit the <i>San Francisco Chronicle</i> was referring to on the front cover), and maybe I just don't know any different. Personally I don't find any sort of disability quite so "witty".<br /><br />Anyway, the story is about four friends from college: Sarah, the narcoleptic; Gregory, the obsessive and freaky boyfriend who wants to be a sleep doctor; Terry, the obsessive and not-so-freaky film buff; and Robert, the obsessive and probably highly confused fan of Sarah's. Other characters come and go, the plot alternates chapter by chapter between the past and the present (whatever, the nineties-present, as the book was published in '97), there are all sorts of heavy connections between all of the characters from beginning to end which makes for a fairly interesting read to see how it all comes around in a giant circle.<br /><br />If O. Henry wrote darker, more ironic stories, this might qualify. Except it's not O. Henry so therefore immediately isn't deemed to be as good. I bounced back and forth while reading - one page made me think it rated as a 3-star book, the next page made me want to rate it as a 2-star book. I think the first half wasn't quite as good as the second part, but really my biggest complaint are the characters - I just couldn't care about them all the time. I wanted to, but some of them are so stupid (Gregory) or so pointless (Terry), and really the only semi-decent parts really involved Sarah and her lesbian phase with Veronica. I just wanted more.<br /><br />But I will say the sleep clinic freaked me the hell out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13509419663809644422" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1611271174" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1611271174" />
    <a title="Ana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39605220-ana"><img alt="Ana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563620297p2/39605220.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1611271174?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ana" href="/user/show/39605220-ana">Ana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39605220-ana?shelf=bought-and-ready-to-be-read">bought-and-ready-to-be-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1611271174" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5467913097232176434">Oh my freakin' duck! This book is how I've imagined LSD on bread would be like. This book is life (now I sound like a tumblrer), everything and the reason why I love reading! I live for this kind of books! Something like this of such majesty, fervour, ingenious depth has to be felt and steered perpetually from end to end of oneself. As those being said, Jonathan Coe is a master of mind tricks enclosed by words and brought to surface by the body's trembling. Left with tears flooding my eyes on th</span>
  <span id="freeText5467913097232176434" style="display:none">Oh my freakin' duck! This book is how I've imagined LSD on bread would be like. This book is life (now I sound like a tumblrer), everything and the reason why I love reading! I live for this kind of books! Something like this of such majesty, fervour, ingenious depth has to be felt and steered perpetually from end to end of oneself. As those being said, Jonathan Coe is a master of mind tricks enclosed by words and brought to surface by the body's trembling. Left with tears flooding my eyes on this one, my synapses nipped, nip which ran through my eyes and my heart (I do feel this whenever I undergo ardent emotions of any kind). Oh yes, I believe the last one stopped for few seconds. <br />I think we all got the idea that this book is about sleep, also all the diseases that sleep denotes. What we, ok... let's say I... didn't know was that this book can open your eyes (bad joke) as far as this is not mostly about sleep (even though I find it quite educative), but our inner self instead. To start with, the book is split into even (the story is taking place in the last two weeks of June, 1996) and uneven chapters (1983-1984). This is the first line in the whole scheme: it makes the far-fetched seem closer, while the whole book is consequently a fulfilment we had all dreamt of and this is to perceive what is not right in some decisions we make and how they tug at our heartstrings in the future when we least expect them to reappear. In 1996, Ashdown turned into a clinic for insomniacs, while in 1983-1984 all the characters gave all out to make a living. From one chapter to another a world hatches right in front of our eyes, dividing the novel into 'the world that is' and 'the world that isn't yet'. The knack that stands at the bottom of the 'smoke and mirrors' are the paths followed, everything knots when no one knows. For instance, to have the same language as the writer (phases of sleep), there was a 'phase' in which they were all working-unconsciously at their own future, during the time that with the use of the chapters' interlacing as a reader you have the eerie feeling that everything was fated (of course there are more and more clues on the road). This is an unnormal state of predictability that I've never read before in a book with such realism, a story that is not on the cards for no one BUT from a source beyond everything (I like to call this fiction), that's why it sends chills on one's spine (becomes embroidered for the sake of harmony). For example: imagine there are many people in a room at a party, they do not want to have anything to do one with another KNOWING unconsciously they will be back in the same place where someday they'll have to talk AND they will for sure. The intensity of this game with the aim of intergrowth is outlandish and bloodcurdling after some time due to the characters. Everything was so carefully wrapped in the cloth of 'dream' that I can barely remember the backgrounds that were not images absorbed from the relation dream-reality. That's because each thing is like a mist, nothing seems touchable since all is absurd, while all revolve around all and all in the void. <br />Second of all, Jonathan Coe gives birth to one of the most topping, deliciously blown up out of all proportion characters to take everything in. The idea of sleep is transmuted into 'ego', whereas the 'self' is distinctive and it floats above each character because yes, this book is a web of fortunes refined by its own mains no matter how far. On this very unique grounding the characters are searching for one another, that's why many of them dream and sense the fate in their reverie as this is what they really want, others reveal how meaningful verity is and others are the 'linkers' between the two worlds. It is like a drawing in which everyone has his/her own place and purpose. I have always been fascinated concerning my own dreams, that's why I had quitted making my own before the real ones. On account of this I could get with all haste to what I wanted, the one that I am not what I want. I don't want to spread spoilers so I won't give any hint of who is who and why. This is the gimmick. All of them try to save what they have including eachother by entering 'life as it is', but the vacillation that delusions give baffle them from following their hearts and own conceptions, combined with their own personality qualm and fear of surroundings. Ashdown can be owning to this change what I like to call 'Land of Oblivion'. <br />Not like it wasn't menacing enough, there are some pieces of twists, love, tragedy, self-hatred... so all can recede in what we can all have... vision. One thing is for sure I will never forget this book. Hopefully I will be able to put all that I've learned in 'actions'. We all want something, but dreaming is not the smartest escape. This book is an escape.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5467913097232176434" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_5540188" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/5540188" />
    <a title="Aaron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/323130-aaron"><img alt="Aaron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1188492019p2/323130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/5540188?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aaron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aaron" href="/user/show/323130-aaron">Aaron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer5540188" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3187099017868702541">There are four major characters in this novel, all of whom knew each other in college. There's Sarah, who suffers from narcolepsy and often cannot discern the events she sees in her dreams from reality. There's Robert, who might be the one affected most by Sarah's disorder (but I can't tell you why without spoiling an awesome twist). There's Terry, film critic and insomniac who claims to not have slept in almost ten years. And Gregory, a world-renowned sleep therapist who believes that sleep is </span>
  <span id="freeText3187099017868702541" style="display:none">There are four major characters in this novel, all of whom knew each other in college. There's Sarah, who suffers from narcolepsy and often cannot discern the events she sees in her dreams from reality. There's Robert, who might be the one affected most by Sarah's disorder (but I can't tell you why without spoiling an awesome twist). There's Terry, film critic and insomniac who claims to not have slept in almost ten years. And Gregory, a world-renowned sleep therapist who believes that sleep is a life-shortening disease that should be eradicated.<br /><br />Jonathan Coe is a writer who remains focused on the details. Several things in this narrative seem unimportant until the end (a scar, an idle conversation). The novel itself is an amalgamation of genre; it's a bit chilling (one of Gregory's experiments is just downright horrifying), more than a little funny (the bit about the misnumbered footnotes makes reading the whole book worthwhile), and effectively layered. However, there's a couple of things that I don't think are explained very well and I find a plot so centered on mere coincidence to be a little problematic. Ultimately, though I enjoyed this novel. It was thought-provoking and handles many different themes effectively. Of these themes, the difference between love and obsession is one of the better drawn out. <br /><br />Highly recommended. I'll be continuing the search for more Jonathan Coe.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3187099017868702541" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3532901474" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3532901474" />
    <a title="Alma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/105050590-alma"><img alt="Alma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606155064p2/105050590.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

  <span id="freeText13725320841923717119" style="display:none">4.7*<br />“ ‘A disease, Terry - the most widespread and life-curtailing disease of all! Forget cancer, forget multiple sclerosis, forget AIDS. If you spend eight hours a day in bed, then sleep is shortening your life by a third! That’s equivalent of dying at the age of fifty- and it’s happening to all of us. This is more than just a disease: this is a plague! And none of us is immune, you realise.” <br />p180<br /><br />Very clever and twisted book about group of people who met in their student years in the eighties and now in after a decade they are drawn back together by problems with their sleep.<br />Terry is insomniac, obsessed with old movies (there is a lot about them!) <br />Sarah is narcoleptic and can’t separate what is real life and what is a dream. Robert is just lost and all his problems started because of Sarah. And there is a doctor who manages the clinic and thinks that we are wasting our life by sleeping.<br />All storyline is changing and unpredictable. I don’t think I have ever read anything like this. Very good humour, some weird sex and an interesting study of sleep. Structure is amazing. I am not sure about the end as it left me hanging. Overall, more experience than just a read<br />Perfect book to read during your sleepless nights! </span>

<div id="review_175445246" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/175445246" />
    <a title="Karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/914730-karen"><img alt="Karen" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/175445246?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen" href="/user/show/914730-karen">Karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer175445246" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6536634968377520046">Two months ago, I picked up a copy of The Terrible Privacy of Maxwell Sim off of a library shelf, and I have become hooked on Jonathan Coe. I think he is brilliant - his writing is immensely creative and funny, his characters are compelling and quirky, his plots are extremely well-crafted, and he always keeps you guessing. He takes risks in the structure of his novels, and while I usually prefer sequential narrative, I think he does an amazing job of telling a story in a non-linear way. It is al</span>
  <span id="freeText6536634968377520046" style="display:none">Two months ago, I picked up a copy of The Terrible Privacy of Maxwell Sim off of a library shelf, and I have become hooked on Jonathan Coe. I think he is brilliant - his writing is immensely creative and funny, his characters are compelling and quirky, his plots are extremely well-crafted, and he always keeps you guessing. He takes risks in the structure of his novels, and while I usually prefer sequential narrative, I think he does an amazing job of telling a story in a non-linear way. It is also SO refreshing to have GLBT themes and characters so well integrated into mainstream literature.<br /><br />As someone with chronic sleep issues, I loved this book. As someone who enjoys satire with a heart, I loved this book. Coe's comic timing is impeccable; the humor leaps out at you when you're not expecting it (eg: "Do you like tortellini?" he asked. Kingsley stared at him defiantly. "Sure I do," he said. "Especially the early, black and white ones.")<br /><br />It is rare that I read books with complex plots where it feels that the author is in complete control of the story, the characters, and the plot; Jonathan Coe is a master. I don't mind his reliance on coincidences; they are not necessarily realistic, but are in the realm of reality, and seem to reflect the interconnectedness of human lives. Reading this book was like putting together a jigsaw puzzle; even though the future is left open-ended, it is immensely satisfying to look at the whole picture in the end.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6536634968377520046" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3467950856338564752">Whenever I write a review for a pseudo-intellectual, surreal story filled with a cast that is both beautifully tragic and surprisingly uplifting in a burdened atmosphere, I become self conscious. Reviewing those types of books is like reviewing Lolita, Nietzsche, or any Hunter Thompson book...readers tend to focus on what you missed, why you don't agree or disagree with <i>their</i> findings and, ultimately, declare you an idiot for not getting the underlining messages hidden throughout the book that <i>t</i></span>
  <span id="freeText3467950856338564752" style="display:none">Whenever I write a review for a pseudo-intellectual, surreal story filled with a cast that is both beautifully tragic and surprisingly uplifting in a burdened atmosphere, I become self conscious. Reviewing those types of books is like reviewing Lolita, Nietzsche, or any Hunter Thompson book...readers tend to focus on what you missed, why you don't agree or disagree with <i>their</i> findings and, ultimately, declare you an idiot for not getting the underlining messages hidden throughout the book that <i>they</i> did. That sounds dramatic and over-reaching, but trust me on this, it's real and it happens ALL THE TIME . (Stop messaging me! Go troll Foxnews or Huffington Post!)<br /><br />So...with all that in mind, I've decided I'm gonna skip the review this time. I don't need that kind of stress in my life. Just trust me and buy this book. It's 50 shades of hallucinatory awesome!</span>

    <a title="Gary Murning" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2518223-gary-murning"><img alt="Gary Murning" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442503170p2/2518223.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/109099926?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gary Murning" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gary Murning" href="/user/show/2518223-gary-murning">Gary Murning</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141033303" href="/book/show/3553078-the-house-of-sleep">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer109099926" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11126405933622706940">A clever, fascinatingly plotted novel, House of Sleep had all the ingredients of a potentially great novel. Well-drawn, intriguing characters, at times vividly descriptive I <i>did</i> enjoy it.<br/><br/>However, I did feel kept at a distance. The multiple viewpoint third person narrative gave it a cinematic quality (apt in many ways, I know) that -- and this is more to do with personal preference -- didn't allow me all the way "in". I have a well-established dislike of novels that switch viewpoint mid-scene, I </span>
  <span id="freeText11126405933622706940" style="display:none">A clever, fascinatingly plotted novel, House of Sleep had all the ingredients of a potentially great novel. Well-drawn, intriguing characters, at times vividly descriptive I <i>did</i> enjoy it.<br /><br />However, I did feel kept at a distance. The multiple viewpoint third person narrative gave it a cinematic quality (apt in many ways, I know) that -- and this is more to do with personal preference -- didn't allow me all the way "in". I have a well-established dislike of novels that switch viewpoint mid-scene, I find it jarring and lazy, and whilst Coe handles these transitions far more skilfully than many, I was nevertheless left with the feeling of watching rather than being properly connected with the characters.<br /><br />That said, an accomplished piece of work. I'll definitely read more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11126405933622706940" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I also think we have that kind of dragged relationship that could be broken up any moment, but it goes on out of habit. <br/>I read the Italian translation of this novel many years ago and I decided to read it again in its original language, but the feeling hasn't changed: too complex for a light reading and not complex enough for a deep reading.   <span id="freeText492513207162738469" style="display:none">I met Coe in my youth and I like him, or I think I do. I also think we have that kind of dragged relationship that could be broken up any moment, but it goes on out of habit. <br />I read the Italian translation of this novel many years ago and I decided to read it again in its original language, but the feeling hasn't changed: too complex for a light reading and not complex enough for a deep reading. I think there is too much going on and in the end many subplot are there to act like a deus ex machina, trying to force a kind of serendipity on the reader. I didn't experience it.<br />On the contrary, I found myself stucked midbook. The beginning and the end are good, if not great, but the central part is sluggish. The plot though is great, the idea behind it original. Unfortunately I fit into the minority of readers who didn't get a good laugh out of it.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12773440355635901867">I picked this up second hand as the blurb looked interesting, only to find out when I got home that the only other book by the same author that I'd read ('The Rain Before it Falls') I'd found disappointing. Hence this book had sat on my shelf unread for six months before I picked it up today. I finished it today too, which is quite indicative of how good a book it is.<br/><br/>The novel consists of alternating chapters set in the mid 1980s and a decade or so later, following a group of students and where </span>
  <span id="freeText12773440355635901867" style="display:none">I picked this up second hand as the blurb looked interesting, only to find out when I got home that the only other book by the same author that I'd read ('The Rain Before it Falls') I'd found disappointing. Hence this book had sat on my shelf unread for six months before I picked it up today. I finished it today too, which is quite indicative of how good a book it is.<br /><br />The novel consists of alternating chapters set in the mid 1980s and a decade or so later, following a group of students and where their lives later took them. There's a great deal of stories interwoven (slightly unbelievably at times) and recurring aspects, but for me it was told in an engaging and also at times very beautiful, intelligent and witty manner.. hence I didn't mind too much about the sense that the plot was a bit contrived. A section on misplaced footnotes was really rather clever indeed, and two or three of the twists were surprising indeed. So I might give Jonathan Coe another try.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_18279975" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18279975" />
    <a title="Gemma Williams" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/633822-gemma-williams"><img alt="Gemma Williams" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576865060p2/633822.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18279975?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gemma Williams" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gemma Williams" href="/user/show/633822-gemma-williams">Gemma Williams</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18279975" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17576234120391254922">I really did enjoy this, although with a few reservations. It is very funny, and the plot is quite ingenious and very interesting. It is a bit over reliant on unlikely coincidence, and for some reason it niggles ; he's not quite good enough to get you to totally suspend your disbelief. Plus, the writer is obviously not a lesbian or a transsexual and doesn't write very convincing characters who are. That aside, this was really very funny with a couple of cracking set pieces. There's a wickedly sh</span>
  <span id="freeText17576234120391254922" style="display:none">I really did enjoy this, although with a few reservations. It is very funny, and the plot is quite ingenious and very interesting. It is a bit over reliant on unlikely coincidence, and for some reason it niggles ; he's not quite good enough to get you to totally suspend your disbelief. Plus, the writer is obviously not a lesbian or a transsexual and doesn't write very convincing characters who are. That aside, this was really very funny with a couple of cracking set pieces. There's a wickedly sharp parody of Lacanian analysis that manages, like all the best such do, to be obviously ridiculous but strangely convincing as well. It does put you off to have the word 'clever' three times on the dust jacket, but it is clever, and made me smile a lot and even laugh out loud twice, and it is well worth a read.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17576234120391254922" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1974763704" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1974763704" />
    <a title="Mikhail Yukhnovskiy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17160618-mikhail-yukhnovskiy"><img alt="Mikhail Yukhnovskiy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360070990p2/17160618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1974763704?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mikhail Yukhnovskiy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mikhail Yukhnovskiy" href="/user/show/17160618-mikhail-yukhnovskiy">Mikhail Yukhnovskiy</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17160618-mikhail-yukhnovskiy?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1974763704" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12542764136835434045">I remember, there were some books that felt as if they were made of the substance of dreams, slow, hazy and beautiful or scary. The House of Sleep is not one of them. It is at the same time much more mundane and more surreal.<br/><br/>The plot centers, and as we later learn revolves around a pretty small group of people who were students sharing accomodation and a building, in which they all lived. The building is in fact The House of Sleep and it is so in more ways than you can imagine. The students arou</span>
  <span id="freeText12542764136835434045" style="display:none">I remember, there were some books that felt as if they were made of the substance of dreams, slow, hazy and beautiful or scary. The House of Sleep is not one of them. It is at the same time much more mundane and more surreal.<br /><br />The plot centers, and as we later learn revolves around a pretty small group of people who were students sharing accomodation and a building, in which they all lived. The building is in fact The House of Sleep and it is so in more ways than you can imagine. The students around whom the book is built each has his or her own special relationship with the sleep. be it narcolepsy, insomnia or building one's life around someone's dreams.<br /><br />The book is well-written and at times hilariously funny, sometimes in a very ironic way. There was at least one moment when I was laughing outloud. However, while the narrative is not what I would call dreamy, the effect of the book is something of an absurdist surreal dream we all sometimes have. Not eveyone will like this. I did like ti though, as I found the narrative serving the purpose of stressing that the life of a person with serious sleep-disorders may truly have an innate absurdity similar to the book.<br /><br />In any case, the main characters either have some sort of trouble sleeping (or with sleeping) or have some very strange dreams.<br /><br />As a conclusion this is a very elegantly written book that some people will be happy to finish reading and to lay aside.<br /><br />Some quotes:<br /><br />“There’s a fine line between forgetting an event, and suppressing the memory of it.” <br /><br />“Objectivity is just male subjectivity.”</span>
  <a data-text-id="12542764136835434045" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Some of the former students have sleep disorders but are not interesting — these sleep disturbances channeled in the minority to where these disorders treated, 12 years later - the same structure that once housed their dormitories.   <span id="freeText15151588577980963992" style="display:none">What is in the book: Some students lived for a certain period in the dormitories. Some of the former students have sleep disorders but are not interesting — these sleep disturbances channeled in the minority to where these disorders treated, 12 years later - the same structure that once housed their dormitories. The director of the sleep lab is one of the heroes of the book, also a former student.<br /><br /><br /> What is not in the book: There is no big and exciting love story, but a small with a bizarre spin. The book is not a comedy, is not amusing, is not funny and doesn't have original and witty tweets — not even fantastic writing. It is a book that tries to be smart with unusual combinations of cases, the flexibility of the plot to improbable laws and in general, although the book somehow flows, it runs nowhere and comes nowhere. </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria Grazia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria Grazia" href="/user/show/3015503-maria-grazia">Maria Grazia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780241967744" href="/book/show/23362868-the-house-of-sleep">review of another edition</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer6660913686817453280">Can a book make you laugh out loud and also make your heart ache? Yes, it happens sometimes and it usually means it's by a great writer. "The House of Sleep" is a clever, brilliant, delightful and touching novel. It was my first Jonathan Coe book, but his brilliancy and intelligence won me and I'm currently reading a second book, The Rain Before It Falls, which is so beautiful and so sad. <br/><br/>"The House of Sleep" is built on two parallel narrative lines telling the stories of the same characters in </span>
  <span id="freeText6660913686817453280" style="display:none">Can a book make you laugh out loud and also make your heart ache? Yes, it happens sometimes and it usually means it's by a great writer. "The House of Sleep" is a clever, brilliant, delightful and touching novel. It was my first Jonathan Coe book, but his brilliancy and intelligence won me and I'm currently reading a second book, The Rain Before It Falls, which is so beautiful and so sad. <br /><br />"The House of Sleep" is built on two parallel narrative lines telling the stories of the same characters in the 1980s and in the 1990s. The odd numbered chapters are set mainly in the years 1983-4 and the even chapters are set in June 1996. The plot develops shifting in time and bit by bit you add the scattered little pieces to the whole jig-saw puzzle which will surprise and move you when you set the last one in place. <br /><br />(from My Summer Time Reads at FLY HIGH! <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://flyhigh-by-learnonline.blogspot.it/2017/08/books-more-books-summertime-reads.html">http://flyhigh-by-learnonline.blogspo...</a> )</span>

<div id="review_139706370" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/139706370" />
    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4401739-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1409827555p2/4401739.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/139706370?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/4401739-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Michelle by: </span>
      Aaron Westermann
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4401739-michelle?shelf=2013-read">2013-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139706370" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5765640687101103055">I have always thought of myself of a stingy awarder of a 5 star rating; alas, I have not been so stingy of late. Jonathan Coe's The House of Sleep is my 6th 5 star rating of 2013. However, being privileged to have so many good friends with such great tastes in literature sure helps stack the bookcase with good reads. The House of Sleep is a favorite of my friend Aaron. Although he and I do not agree upon the greatness of every book, we definitely agree on the greatness of Coe's House of Sleep.<br/><br/>Th</span>
  <span id="freeText5765640687101103055" style="display:none">I have always thought of myself of a stingy awarder of a 5 star rating; alas, I have not been so stingy of late. Jonathan Coe's The House of Sleep is my 6th 5 star rating of 2013. However, being privileged to have so many good friends with such great tastes in literature sure helps stack the bookcase with good reads. The House of Sleep is a favorite of my friend Aaron. Although he and I do not agree upon the greatness of every book, we definitely agree on the greatness of Coe's House of Sleep.<br /><br />The book takes place near London in the years 1983-1984 and June 1996. It centers around the lives of 4 people who attended college together and roomed at Ashdown, an imposing old home on the cliffs near the University. Coe remarkably weaves his story of the lives of these students and more using well developed dialog, humor and suspense. There were times I literally laughed out loud guffawing while reading this book in multiple airports across the US while bored frequent flyers looked at me like I was crazy! Many characters in the book have psychological issues mainly related to sleep issues - narcolepsy, somniloquy and sleep deprivation to name a few. Interestingly, it was my inability to sleep while flying that enabled me to finish this book in such a short time. Which is the only good thing about multiple delays (over 6 hours of delays for a flight that was supposed to take only 6 hours) while attempting to fly across country.<br /><br />Coe expertly uses well written dialog to not only tell the story but to fully define his characters. At the same time he has constructed a plot line with so many twists and turns that the reader has no idea where the book is going even as he turns the last page. Coe alternates his chapters by years but each chapter may have multiple points of view. One technique he uses is the transcript between a character and their shrink. Another interesting technique was to end a chapter mid sentence in the 80s and start the next chapter taking place in the 90s mid sentence as well. Reading this book in both paper and e-book, I had to make sure that I was not missing pages in either.<br /><br />The House of Sleep is a fun filled, fast pace, page turner with a hint of a little romance. Unfortunately it was written in the late 90s so many of my friends have not read it. Find it if you can so I will have someone to discuss it with! It is well worth the time!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5765640687101103055" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_189886520" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/189886520" />
    <a title="Robert" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2744544-robert"><img alt="Robert" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465764198p2/2744544.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/189886520?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robert" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robert" href="/user/show/2744544-robert">Robert</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140250831" href="/book/show/828373.The_House_of_Sleep">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer189886520" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12721480293444470159">Jonathan Coe set a high standard with What a Carve Up! so I wasn’t so sure that my reread of House of Sleep would live up to that book. The fact that I forgot most of it is a telltale sign. There was no need to worry. If anything The House of Sleep is equally good.<br/><br/>Jonathan Coe is an eclectic author. Sure he does have some themes that are commonplace : politics, love’s power, music and a couple of disturbing moments. However, he is clever enough to disguise them with an original plot.<br/><br/>Sarah is nar</span>
  <span id="freeText12721480293444470159" style="display:none">Jonathan Coe set a high standard with What a Carve Up! so I wasn’t so sure that my reread of House of Sleep would live up to that book. The fact that I forgot most of it is a telltale sign. There was no need to worry. If anything The House of Sleep is equally good.<br /><br />Jonathan Coe is an eclectic author. Sure he does have some themes that are commonplace : politics, love’s power, music and a couple of disturbing moments. However, he is clever enough to disguise them with an original plot.<br /><br />Sarah is narcoleptic. To make matters worse she cannot distinguish between her dreams and reality, which land her in uncomfortable situations. Terry is a movie fanatic insomniac. These two characters are linked by Robert, who is a friend of Terry’s and has an obsessive (but not creepy) crush on Sarah. Those are the odd numbered chapters.<br /><br />The even numbered chapters take place twelve years later and Terry has been noticed by Dr. Gregory Dudden who wants to perform experiments on him in his sleep clinic. Past meets present and all of Sarah’s and Terry’s actions are now suffering the repercussions of their childhood actions.<br /><br />The House of Sleep is a multi layered novel. As us readers continue to discover Sarah, Robert and Terry’s antics, the novel becomes richer. It is an unpredictable book as well, with constant plot twists. As always, Coe is clever but remains accessible. The House of Sleep is an easy read but does need a couple of moments to digest the surprises which occur. That’s not mentioning the madcap ending!<br /><br />The novel is a little bit of a curio. It is definitely not Coe’s most political novel, aside from a few jabs at the British healthcare system. It’s not grisly either. However it is Coe’s overt statement about love and how it can unite and destroy. In one case even change a person. Which goes to show what a versatile author Coe is. The next book is a heavily political one so let’s how that goes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12721480293444470159" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1563749197" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1563749197" />
    <a title="Lee Foust" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13984676-lee-foust"><img alt="Lee Foust" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442875445p2/13984676.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1563749197?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lee Foust" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lee Foust" href="/user/show/13984676-lee-foust">Lee Foust</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780241967744" href="/book/show/23362868-the-house-of-sleep">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1563749197" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10360502442377925835">Yes, it's clever, often funny, and even touching--but I can't help feeling that <i>The House of Sleep</i> is just a tiny bit too much of each of these things. It's also the second book I've read in a row where I feel loath to discourse upon it in print because it would be something of a disservice to a prospective reader. Best to jump into this one with no expectations and let it take you where it will without having any signposts. Yes, it's worth it (4 stars for me means a good book, 5 is great and 3 </span>
  <span id="freeText10360502442377925835" style="display:none">Yes, it's clever, often funny, and even touching--but I can't help feeling that <i>The House of Sleep</i> is just a tiny bit too much of each of these things. It's also the second book I've read in a row where I feel loath to discourse upon it in print because it would be something of a disservice to a prospective reader. Best to jump into this one with no expectations and let it take you where it will without having any signposts. Yes, it's worth it (4 stars for me means a good book, 5 is great and 3 just average).<br /><br />The novel goes fast and the overall architecture is quite good, but also rather an obvious literary edifice. Still, that goes with the rest of the narrative, as we're in a world just a little too artistically articulated to be quite real--too many coincidences and too much obvious meaning in everything that happens. Should Coe have gone further? (more postmodern or more magical in his magic realism?) Or should he have domesticated this more towards a believably realistic narrative? I'm not sure. For him we must assume that this is the perfect balance he wanted to achieve between the real and the artificial in this particular narrative and that's admirable in an author. He stuck to his vision. Like all works of art, then, it's up to your taste as a reader, really, to allow yourself to enjoy the book's obvious artifice or to find it annoyingly ordered and improbable. I rushed right through with a minimum of pain--but I was never 100% convinced of the novel's stab at genius. Looking forward to Coe's impending visit to Florence and to reading more of his novels though. In the end it was more intriguing to me than anything else.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10360502442377925835" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2750533910" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2750533910" />
    <a title="Debbie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5273282-debbie"><img alt="Debbie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472672896p2/5273282.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2750533910?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debbie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debbie" href="/user/show/5273282-debbie">Debbie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2750533910" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6035043855329469374">First and for most you have to know something about this book. It contains horrific animal cruelty. <br/><br/>And I mean absolutely horrific. If I had known this I would not have picked the book up. I certainly couldn’t read it after a few sentences . It made me feel sick and very upset. I have an incredibly low tolerance for animal cruelty and I couldn’t bear it.<br/><br/>It’s a good book but that override everything and was too much for me.<br/><br/>I remember reading another one of his that also had extreme animal cruelty</span>
  <span id="freeText6035043855329469374" style="display:none">First and for most you have to know something about this book. It contains horrific animal cruelty. <br /><br />And I mean absolutely horrific. If I had known this I would not have picked the book up. I certainly couldn’t read it after a few sentences . It made me feel sick and very upset. I have an incredibly low tolerance for animal cruelty and I couldn’t bear it.<br /><br />It’s a good book but that override everything and was too much for me.<br /><br />I remember reading another one of his that also had extreme animal cruelty that to this day I can’t get out of my head. It really upset me and although the book was 5 stars I wish I hadn’t read it. I feel the same way about this book. Sometimes I need to shield myself from horrible things and although it’s a fascinating book. Those few pages are something I wish I hadn’t read because I’m not capable of dealing with them.<br /><br /> it definitely needs a trigger warning<br /><br /> One of the redeeming sections is the article with the incorrect footnotes. That is a great bit of fun writing and almost completely at odds with the rest of the book, to the point where it works. <br /><br />However. All I could think was, you know what’s going on right now and not a part of you feels like you need to put a stop to it. Your quite happy to let the ‘experiment’ go on and not give it a second thought? <br /><br />It was too much for me, and I don’t think it was necessary to the story at all. I’m actually fairly angry about it. I’ll end up with nightmares over something that wasn’t required for the plot. Without that I’d have given it 3 stars but I can only give it 2 because it’s going to stay with me for all the wrong reasons.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1913342620" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1913342620" />
    <a title="Carol Fenlon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1600622-carol-fenlon"><img alt="Carol Fenlon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442483534p2/1600622.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1913342620?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol Fenlon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol Fenlon" href="/user/show/1600622-carol-fenlon">Carol Fenlon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1913342620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6442442307666200375">Opened this with great expectations, being a big fan of Coe. I have to say I found it a bit harder to get into than some of his other novels. I got a bit confused with all the characters and the time shifts but I got used to it in the end. I didn't feel a great deal of empathy for the characters at first but towards the end I started to feel for Robert and Sarah and I was glad it ended as it did. There are certainly plenty of surprises and the many devices of form so characteristic of Coe kept m</span>
  <span id="freeText6442442307666200375" style="display:none">Opened this with great expectations, being a big fan of Coe. I have to say I found it a bit harder to get into than some of his other novels. I got a bit confused with all the characters and the time shifts but I got used to it in the end. I didn't feel a great deal of empathy for the characters at first but towards the end I started to feel for Robert and Sarah and I was glad it ended as it did. There are certainly plenty of surprises and the many devices of form so characteristic of Coe kept me intrigued and entertained throughout. There is always the difficulty though that the reader can get wrapped up in admiring the writing and lose the plot which I did at times, having to backtrack to recall what had gone one (fortunately I was reading the paperback so that was easy enough). There were the usual moments of total hilarity due to the author's pyrotechnics with wordplay. Of note are the descriptions of Gregory and Sarah's sexual relations (hysterical) and Coe excels himself with the spoof journal article 'Fragments from a life in the movies' where the footnotes have been accidentally changed so that they apply to the wrong people. Thankfully I was at home when I read this or I would have been locked up as I cried so much with laughter, I was quite exhausted.<br />I still have several Coe novels to read and i am trying to save them by interspersing them with other novels on my wish list. It's great to find an author you love, who is a prolific producer so that there are many books to enjoy. This has been just one of them</span>
  <a data-text-id="6442442307666200375" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_191231872" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/191231872" />
    <a title="Derek James Baldwin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2200252-derek-james-baldwin"><img alt="Derek James Baldwin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311872110p2/2200252.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/191231872?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Derek James Baldwin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Derek James Baldwin" href="/user/show/2200252-derek-james-baldwin">Derek James Baldwin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer191231872" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1650053468247662949">Very enjoyable novel that messes you around just enough in the early chapters to intrigue you into keeping reading, then draws all the threads together very neatly. The fact that the story is so openly contrived might irritate some, but I appreciated the author's efforts even if some of the deeper points he might have been trying to make aren't fully realised. There are some marvellously funny moments along the way, in particular Terry Worth's dialogue with an irritating tyro American film direc</span>
  <span id="freeText1650053468247662949" style="display:none">Very enjoyable novel that messes you around just enough in the early chapters to intrigue you into keeping reading, then draws all the threads together very neatly. The fact that the story is so openly contrived might irritate some, but I appreciated the author's efforts even if some of the deeper points he might have been trying to make aren't fully realised. There are some marvellously funny moments along the way, in particular Terry Worth's dialogue with an irritating tyro American film director with a scant regard for European "art cinema". A (fictional) Portuguese film director's lost masterpiece plays a critical role, and the whole theme of cinema/fantasy/dream is neatly realised. The Lacanian psychiatrist's case study is another very funny and deadly accurate satire, possibly one which film theorists will especially appreciate (c.f. Laura Mulvey's theories on the "male gaze" in cinema, for example). The novel flicks between ten years ago and the present day very neatly too. Really my only reservation at all is the grand guignol scene near the end when sleep expert Gregory Dudden enters full-on mad scientist mode. But I warmly recommend this, very definitely worth reading. If you've ever studied psychology, cinema, or both, you will especially enjoy it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1650053468247662949" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dXiS8qIbl3DWV7Ijp16BsXR06BXxAfxlavnvPH2NPuVNCGFn8SEs6ygtrLgH8+LNlcfTlkbm+J8/PNAxhx+fYw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ofICRj2UegWYV+EuWHSnwHq0emOkE1NGVss5xkw9T2uZgvHTbq7BnmYt/7X42cS8mwdB4BP0V7wDDgbLtq/u7Q==')})
  }

Детей рисовать труднее всего, потому что они все время вертятся. Постоянно получается так, что у меня на бумаге четыре ноги и три руки. Но если подумать, это ведь правда: когда мы сидим, у нас ног две, а когда бежим – двенадцать. Когда я рисую, никто меня не замечает».\n«Я купил себе маркер и стал ходить по району и рисовать, ну, там, где видно, разных человечков… Потом я стал часто встречать этих чуваков, которых я нарисовал на стенах, я вспоминал, как я каждого из них нарисовал, и мне становилось теплее».\nКсения Букша тоже рисует человека одним штрихом, одной точной фразой. <span id="freeTextContainer15685505161507591138"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces' rel='nofollow noopener'>See this thread for more information.</a> </i> <br/><br/>Jonathan Coe, born 19 August 1961 in Birmingham, is a British novelist and writer. His work usually has an underlying preoccupation with political issues, although this serious engagement is often expressed comically in the form of satire. For example, What a Carve Up! rew</span>
  <span id="freeText15685505161507591138" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces" rel="nofollow noopener">See this thread for more information.</a> </i> <br /><br />Jonathan Coe, born 19 August 1961 in Birmingham, is a British novelist and writer. His work usually has an underlying preoccupation with political issues, although this serious engagement is often expressed comically in the form of satire. For example, What a Carve Up! reworks the plot of an old 1960s spoof horror film of the same name, in the light of the 'carve up' of the UK's resources which some felt was carried out by Margaret Thatcher's right wing Conservative governments of the 1980s. Coe studied at King Edward's School, Birmingham and Trinity College, Cambridge, before teaching at the University of Warwick where he completed a PhD in English Literature. In July 2006 he was given an honorary degree by The University of Birmingham.<br /><br />-<br />Retrieved 10:55, February 2, 2009 from <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jonathan_Coe">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jonathan...</a><br /><br /></span>
